SMARTdenovo v1.0<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 40" title="Jue, R. smartdenovo: ultra-fast de novo assembler using long noisy reads. &#xA;                  https://github.com/ruanjue/smartdenovo&#xA;                  &#xA;                 (2015)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00382-1#ref-CR40" id="ref-link-section-d50938e3131">40</a></sup> was the third tool used for the assembly. The results of the assemblies were efficiently merged using Quickmerge v0.2.2<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 41" title="Chakraborty, M. et al. Contiguous and accurate de novo assembly of metazoan genomes with modest long read coverage. Nucleic Acids Res. 44, 147â151 (2016)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00382-1#ref-CR41" id="ref-link-section-d50938e3136">41</a></sup>, and the redundant data were removed with Numer v4.0.0<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 42" title="Kurtz, S. et al. Versatile and open software for comparing large genomes. Genome Biol. 5, 12â15 (2004)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00382-1#ref-CR42" id="ref-link-section-d50938e3140">42</a></sup>. The consensus of the merged assembly as input was polished and corrected three times using Racon<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 30" title="Vaser, R. et al. Fast and accurate de novo genome assembly from long uncorrected reads. Genome Res. 5, 27â32 (2017)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00382-1#ref-CR30" id="ref-link-section-d50938e3144">30</a></sup>. Moreover, Illumina reads specifically for genome feature estimation were prepared for the correction of the final assembly using Pilon v1.22<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 43" title="Walker, B. J. et al. Pilon: an integrated tool for comprehensive microbial variant detection and genome assembly improvement. PLoS ONE 9, 29â32 (2014)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00382-1#ref-CR43" id="ref-link-section-d50938e3148">43</a></sup>, which also performed three corrections.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading c-article__sub-heading--divider" id="Sec16">Hi-C scaffolding</h3><p>An assembled genome can be perfectly identified by chromatin interactions using the Hi-C technique. A total of 122.84 million clean reads were mapped to the primary assembly by Nanopore long reads using BWA aligner v0.7.10-r789<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 44" title="Li, H. Aligning sequence reads, clone sequences and assembly contigs with BWA-MEM. Genomics. 3, 76â78 (2013)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00382-1#ref-CR44" id="ref-link-section-d50938e3161">44</a></sup> with the default parameters. In cases where both ends of the paired reads mapped to the assembly, only reads of the two pairs that were uniquely mapped were used for further analysis. There were two different types of mapped paired reads obtained by assessing self-circle ligation, dangling ends, and religation: valid interaction pairs and invalid interaction pairs. To obtain valid interactive Hi-C reads, reads of self-ligation, nonligation, dangling ends, and other invalid reads were filtered and removed using Hi-C-Pro v2.10.0<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 45" title="Servant, N. et al. HiC-Pro: an optimized and flexible pipeline for Hi-C data processing. Genome Biol. 16, 1â11 (2015)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00382-1#ref-CR45" id="ref-link-section-d50938e3165">45</a></sup>.</p><p>The contigs of the primary assembly were broken into 50-kb fragments normalized by the restriction sites. Candidate chromosomes were then generated automatically, and the reassembled contigs were divided into ordered, oriented, and anchored groups using Lachesis v2e27abb<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 46" title="Burton, J. N. et al. Chromosome-scale scaffolding of de novo genome assemblies based on chromatin interactions. Nat. Biotechnol. 31, 1119â1125 (2013)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00382-1#ref-CR46" id="ref-link-section-d50938e3172">46</a></sup> with the following parameters: CLUSTER_MIN_RE_SITESâ=â37, CLUSTER_MAX_LINK_DENSITYâ=â2, CLUSTER_NONINFORMATIVE_RATIOâ=â2, ORDER_MIN_N_RES_IN_TRUNâ=â33, and ORDER_MIN_N_RES_IN_SHREDSâ=â31. To further improve the assembly of Hi-C, gaps in the Hi-C assembly were filled using LR GapCloser v1.1<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 47" title="Xu, G. C. et al. LR Gapcloser: a tiling path-based gap closer that uses long reads to complete genome assembly. Gigascience 8, 157â160 (2018)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00382-1#ref-CR47" id="ref-link-section-d50938e3176">47</a></sup>.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading c-article__sub-heading--divider" id="Sec17">Genome-quality evaluation</h3><p>BUSCO v4.0.6<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 48" title="SimÃ£o, F. A. et al. BUSCO: assessing genome assembly and annotation completeness with single-copy orthologs. Bioinformatics 31, 19â23 (2015)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00382-1#ref-CR48" id="ref-link-section-d50938e3188">48</a></sup> and CEGMA v2.5<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 49" title="Parra, G., Bradnam, K. &amp; Korf, I. CEGMA: a pipeline to accurately annotate core genes in eukaryotic genomes. Bioinformatics 23, 1061â1067 (2007)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00382-1#ref-CR49" id="ref-link-section-d50938e3192">49</a></sup> are two tools frequently used to evaluate the level of final genome completeness. The Illumina reads for the genome survey were mapped to the final assembled genome using SAMtools v0.1.18<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 50" title="Li, H. et al. The sequence alignment/map format and SAMtools. Bioinformatics 25, 2078â2079 (2009)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00382-1#ref-CR50" id="ref-link-section-d50938e3196">50</a></sup>. Considering that it had low conservativeness in interspecies repeat sequences, it was necessary to construct a specific repetitive sequence database of <i>C. serrulata</i> for repeat predictions. Repetitive sequences of the <i>C. serrulata</i> genome were first predicted using LTR FINDER v1.05<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 51" title="Xu, Z. &amp; Wang, H. LTR FINDER: an efficient tool for the prediction of full-length LTR retrotransposons. Nucleic Acids Res. 35, 265â268 (2007)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00382-1#ref-CR51" id="ref-link-section-d50938e3207">51</a></sup>, RepeatScout v1.0.5<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 52" title="Price, A. L., Jones, N. C. &amp; Pevzner, P. A. De novo identification of repeat families in large genomes. Bioinformatics 21, 351â358 (2005)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00382-1#ref-CR52" id="ref-link-section-d50938e3211">52</a></sup>, and PILER-DF v2.4<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 53" title="Edgar, R. C. &amp; Myers, E. W. PILER: identification and classification of genomic repeats. Bioinformatics 21, 152â158 (2005)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00382-1#ref-CR53" id="ref-link-section-d50938e3215">53</a></sup>, and DNA repeats were identified and classified using PASTEClassifier v1.0<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 54" title="Wicker, T. et al. A unified classification system for eukaryotic transposable elements. Nat. Rev. Genet. 8, 973â982 (2007)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00382-1#ref-CR54" id="ref-link-section-d50938e3219">54</a></sup>. When the predictions and Repbase results were combined, a final repeat database for only <i>C. serrulata</i> was generated using RepeatMasker v4.0.7<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 55" title="Smit, A., Hubley. R. &amp; Green, P. RepeatMasker Open-4.0 (2013-2015). &#xA;                  http://repeatmasker.org&#xA;                  &#xA;                 (2017)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00382-1#ref-CR55" id="ref-link-section-d50938e3226">55</a></sup>.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading c-article__sub-heading--divider" id="Sec18">Genome annotation</h3><p>Protein-coding gene prediction was performed using three classic strategies: ab initio prediction, homology-based prediction, and transcriptome-based prediction. For ab initio prediction, five tools, GenScan v3.1<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 56" title="Burge, C. &amp; Karlin, S. Prediction of complete gene structures in human genomic DNA. J. Mol. Biol. 268, 78â94 (1997)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00382-1#ref-CR56" id="ref-link-section-d50938e3238">56</a></sup>, Augustus v3.1<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 57" title="Stanke, M. &amp; Waack, S. Gene prediction with a hidden Markov model and a new intron submodel. Bioinformatics 19, 215â225 (2003)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00382-1#ref-CR57" id="ref-link-section-d50938e3242">57</a></sup>, GlimmerHMM v1.2<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 58" title="Majoros, W. H. et al. Two open source ab initio eukaryotic gene-finders. Bioinformatics 20, 2878â2879 (2004)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00382-1#ref-CR58" id="ref-link-section-d50938e3246">58</a></sup>, Gene ID v1.4<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 59" title="Blanco, E., Parra, G. &amp; GuigÃ³, R. Using geneid to identify genes. Curr. Protoc Bioinform. 18, 1â28 (2007)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00382-1#ref-CR59" id="ref-link-section-d50938e3250">59</a></sup>, and SNAP v2006-07-28<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 60" title="Korf, I. Gene finding in novel genomes. BMC Bioinform. 5, 59â62 (2004)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00382-1#ref-CR60" id="ref-link-section-d50938e3254">60</a></sup>, were used to predict the coding genes with model training by turn. For homology-based prediction, protein sequences from five representative species (<i>Arabidopsis thaliana</i><sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 61" title="Meyerowitz, E. M. Arabidopsis thaliana. Ann. Rev. Genet. 21, 93â111 (2003)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00382-1#ref-CR61" id="ref-link-section-d50938e3261">61</a></sup>, <i>Prunus persica</i><sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 13" title="Verde, I. et al. The high-quality draft genome of peach (Prunus persica) identifies unique patterns of genetic diversity, domestication and genome evolution. Nat. Genet. 45, 487â494 (2013)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00382-1#ref-CR13" id="ref-link-section-d50938e3267">13</a></sup>, <i>Malus domestica</i><sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 14" title="Velasco, R. et al. The genome of the domesticated apple (Malus x domestica). Nat. Genet. 42, 833â839 (2010)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00382-1#ref-CR14" id="ref-link-section-d50938e3273">14</a></sup>, <i>Prunus dulcis</i><sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 15" title="Velasco, D. et al. Evolutionary genomics of peach and almond domestication. G3 32, 116â121 (2016)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00382-1#ref-CR15" id="ref-link-section-d50938e3279">15</a></sup>, and <i>Rubus occidentalis</i><sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 18" title="Vanburen, R. et al. The genome of black raspberry (Rubus occidentalis). Plant J. 87, 535â547 (2016)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00382-1#ref-CR18" id="ref-link-section-d50938e3286">18</a></sup>) were downloaded from databases and aligned to the <i>C. serrulata</i> protein sequences using GeMoMa v1.3.1<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 62" title="Keilwagen, J. et al. Using intron position conservation for homology-based gene prediction. Nucleic Acids Res. 44, 89â95 (2016)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00382-1#ref-CR62" id="ref-link-section-d50938e3293">62</a></sup>. For transcriptome-based prediction, transcriptome sequencing data obtained in a previous study were used for predicting genes using HISAT v2.0.4<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 63" title="Pertea, M. et al. Transcript-level expression analysis of RNA-seq experiments with HISAT, StringTie and Ballgown. Nat. Protoc. 11, 1650â1658 (2016)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00382-1#ref-CR63" id="ref-link-section-d50938e3297">63</a></sup>, StringTie v1.2.3<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 63" title="Pertea, M. et al. Transcript-level expression analysis of RNA-seq experiments with HISAT, StringTie and Ballgown. Nat. Protoc. 11, 1650â1658 (2016)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00382-1#ref-CR63" id="ref-link-section-d50938e3301">63</a></sup>, TransDecoder v2.0<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 64" title="Haas, B. J. &amp; Papanicolaou, A. TransDecoder (Find Coding Regions Within Transcripts). &#xA;                  http://transdecoder.github.io&#xA;                  &#xA;                 (2015)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00382-1#ref-CR64" id="ref-link-section-d50938e3306">64</a></sup>, and GeneMark v5.1<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 65" title="Tang, S., Lomsadze, A. &amp; Borodovsky, M. Identification of protein coding regions in RNA transcripts. Nucleic Acids Res. 43, 78â85 (2015)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00382-1#ref-CR65" id="ref-link-section-d50938e3310">65</a></sup> according to the respective workflows. Three classic prediction strategies were subsequently integrated into nonredundant protein-coding genes using EVM v1.1.1<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 66" title="Haas, B. J. et al. Automated eukaryotic gene structure annotation using EVidenceModeler and the Program to Assemble Spliced Alignments. Genome Biol. 9, 7â15 (2008)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00382-1#ref-CR66" id="ref-link-section-d50938e3314">66</a></sup> and then modified by PASA v2.0.2<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 67" title="Campbell, M. A. et al. Comprehensive analysis of alternative splicing in rice and comparative analyses with Arabidopsis. BMC Genomics 7, 324â327 (2006)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00382-1#ref-CR67" id="ref-link-section-d50938e3318">67</a></sup>.</p><p>Pseudogenes and noncoding RNAs, including microRNA, ribosomal RNA (rRNA), and transfer RNA (tRNA), were identified and assessed during this step. In the process of searching for putative pseudogenes, they were assessed based on the premature stop codons or frameshift mutations within the structure of genes using GenBlastA v1.0.4<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 68" title="She, R. et al. genBlastG: using BLAST searches to build homologous gene models. Bioinformatics 27, 2141â2143 (2011)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00382-1#ref-CR68" id="ref-link-section-d50938e3325">68</a></sup> and GeneWise v2.4.1<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 69" title="Nawrocki, E. P. &amp; Eddy, S. R. Infernal 1.1: 100-fold faster RNA homology searches. Bioinformatics 29, 2933â2935 (2013)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00382-1#ref-CR69" id="ref-link-section-d50938e3329">69</a></sup>. MicroRNA and rRNA were identified by Infernal 1.1<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 69" title="Nawrocki, E. P. &amp; Eddy, S. R. Infernal 1.1: 100-fold faster RNA homology searches. Bioinformatics 29, 2933â2935 (2013)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00382-1#ref-CR69" id="ref-link-section-d50938e3333">69</a></sup> based on information from miRBase<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 70" title="Griffiths, J. S. et al. miRBase: microRNA sequences, targets and gene nomenclature. Nucleic Acids Res. 34, 140â144 (2006)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00382-1#ref-CR70" id="ref-link-section-d50938e3337">70</a></sup> and Rfam<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 71" title="Griffiths, J. S. et al. Rfam: annotating non-coding RNAs in complete genomes. Nucleic Acids Res. 33, 121â124 (2005)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00382-1#ref-CR71" id="ref-link-section-d50938e3341">71</a></sup>, respectively, and the tRNA was identified using tRNAscan-SE v1.3.1<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 72" title="Lowe, T. M. &amp; Eddy, S. R. tRNAscan-SE: a program for improved detection of transfer RNAgenes in genomic sequence. Nucleic Acids Res. 25, 955â964 (1997)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00382-1#ref-CR72" id="ref-link-section-d50938e3346">72</a></sup>.</p><p>Based on the sequence similarity and domain conservation, protein-coding genes were annotated by aligning to the EuKaryotic Orthologous Groups (KOG)<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 73" title="Tatusov, R. L. et al. The COG database: new developments in phylogenetic classification of proteins from complete genomes. Nucleic Acids Res. 29, 22â28 (2001)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00382-1#ref-CR73" id="ref-link-section-d50938e3353">73</a></sup>, Kyoto Encyclopedia of Genes and Genomes (KEGG)<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 74" title="Kanehisa, M. &amp; Goto, S. KEGG: kyoto encyclopedia of genes and genomes. Nucleic Acids Res. 28, 27â30 (2000)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00382-1#ref-CR74" id="ref-link-section-d50938e3357">74</a></sup>, TrEMBL<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 75" title="Boeckmann, B. et al. The SWISS-PROT protein knowledgebase and its supplement TrEMBL in 2003. Nucleic Acids Res. 31, 365â370 (2003)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00382-1#ref-CR75" id="ref-link-section-d50938e3361">75</a></sup>, Swiss-Prot<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 75" title="Boeckmann, B. et al. The SWISS-PROT protein knowledgebase and its supplement TrEMBL in 2003. Nucleic Acids Res. 31, 365â370 (2003)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00382-1#ref-CR75" id="ref-link-section-d50938e3365">75</a></sup>, and Nonredundant (Nr) databases<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 76" title="Marchler, B. A. et al. CDD: a conserved domain database for the functional annotation of proteins. Nucleic Acids Res. 39, 225â229 (2011)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00382-1#ref-CR76" id="ref-link-section-d50938e3369">76</a></sup> using BLAST v2.2.31<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 36" title="Altschul, S. F. et al. Basic local alignment search tool. J. Mol. Biol. 215, 403â410 (1990)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00382-1#ref-CR36" id="ref-link-section-d50938e3374">36</a></sup>, with a maximal E-value of 1e<sup>â05</sup>. Additionally, functional genes were identified and searched by aligning to the Pfam database<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 77" title="El, G. S. et al. The Pfam protein families database in 2019. Nucleic Acids Res. 47, 427â432 (2019)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00382-1#ref-CR77" id="ref-link-section-d50938e3380">77</a></sup> sequences and Gene Ontology (GO) terms<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 78" title="Dimmer, E. C. et al. The UniProt-GO annotation database in 2011. Nucleic Acids Res. 40, 565â570 (2012)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00382-1#ref-CR78" id="ref-link-section-d50938e3384">78</a></sup> using HMMER V3.0<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 79" title="Eddy, S. R., Mitchison, G. &amp; Durbin, R. Maximum discrimination hidden Markov models of sequence consensus. J. Comput. Biol. 2, 9â23 (1995)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00382-1#ref-CR79" id="ref-link-section-d50938e3388">79</a></sup> and the BLAST2GO v2.5 pipeline<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 80" title="Conesa, A. et al. Blast2GO: a universal tool for annotation, visualization and analysis in functional genomics research. Bioinformatics 21, 3674â3676 (2005)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00382-1#ref-CR80" id="ref-link-section-d50938e3392">80</a></sup>, respectively.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading c-article__sub-heading--divider" id="Sec19">Synteny analysis</h3><p><i>Cerasus</i> species can be divided into those that are cultivated for their flowers and those that are cultivated for their fruit, as represented by <i>C. serrulata</i> and <i>C. avium</i> (<i>Cerasus avium</i>), respectively. The genome of <i>P. persica</i> (<i>Prunus persica</i>) has been widely used for its high-quality assembly. In this analysis, the genome sequence of two species with a chromosomal-level assembly, those of <i>P. persica</i> (<i>Prunus</i> L.)<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 13" title="Verde, I. et al. The high-quality draft genome of peach (Prunus persica) identifies unique patterns of genetic diversity, domestication and genome evolution. Nat. Genet. 45, 487â494 (2013)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00382-1#ref-CR13" id="ref-link-section-d50938e3428">13</a></sup> and <i>C. avium</i><sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 12" title="Shirasawa, K. et al. The genome sequence of sweet cherry (Prunus avium) for use in genomics-assisted breeding. DNA Research. 24, 499â508 (2017)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00382-1#ref-CR12" id="ref-link-section-d50938e3434">12</a></sup>, were downloaded from databases and compared with the genome sequence of <i>C. serrulata</i>. The final chromosomes of <i>C. serrulata</i> were considered to be arranged in the best order by referring to the recognized <i>P. persica</i> genome. For collinearity analysis, we compared the <i>C. serrulata</i> genome with the genomes of <i>P. persica</i> and <i>C. avium</i> using MUMmer (<a href="http://mummer.sourceforge.net">http://mummer.sourceforge.net</a>), with the parameter lâ=â10,000. In addition, the genomes of <i>C. serrulata</i> and <i>C. avium</i> were subjected to a synteny analysis to reveal syntenic blocks in detail and the associated genes using BLASTP (<i>E</i>â&lt;â1e<sup>â05</sup>)<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 36" title="Altschul, S. F. et al. Basic local alignment search tool. J. Mol. Biol. 215, 403â410 (1990)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00382-1#ref-CR36" id="ref-link-section-d50938e3476">36</a></sup>. Each syntenic block comprising at least five sequential genes with no obvious error is displayed in the synteny map.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading c-article__sub-heading--divider" id="Sec20">Gene family identification</h3><p>To identify gene families from the protein-coding genes, protein sequences from <i>C. serrulata</i> and other representative species, including <i>C. avium</i><sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 12" title="Shirasawa, K. et al. The genome sequence of sweet cherry (Prunus avium) for use in genomics-assisted breeding. DNA Research. 24, 499â508 (2017)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00382-1#ref-CR12" id="ref-link-section-d50938e3493">12</a></sup>, <i>P. persica</i><sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 13" title="Verde, I. et al. The high-quality draft genome of peach (Prunus persica) identifies unique patterns of genetic diversity, domestication and genome evolution. Nat. Genet. 45, 487â494 (2013)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00382-1#ref-CR13" id="ref-link-section-d50938e3499">13</a></sup>, <i>P. dulcis</i> (<i>Prunus dulcis</i>)<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 15" title="Velasco, D. et al. Evolutionary genomics of peach and almond domestication. G3 32, 116â121 (2016)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00382-1#ref-CR15" id="ref-link-section-d50938e3510">15</a></sup>, <i>P. mume</i> (<i>Prunus mume</i>)<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 20" title="Zhang, Q. et al. The genome of Prunus mume. Nat. Commun. 3, 1318â1325 (2012)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00382-1#ref-CR20" id="ref-link-section-d50938e3520">20</a></sup>, <i>P. yedoensis</i> (<i>Prunus yedoensis</i>)<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 19" title="Seunghoon, B. et al. Draft genome sequence of wild Prunus yedoensis reveals massive inter-specific hybridization between sympatric flowering cherries. Genome Biol. 19, 45â51 (2018)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00382-1#ref-CR19" id="ref-link-section-d50938e3531">19</a></sup>, <i>R. chinensis</i> (<i>Rosa chinensis</i>)<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 21" title="Lin, W. et al. Characterization of the complete chloroplast genome of Chinese rose, Rosa chinensis (Rosaceae: Rosa). Mitochondrial DNA B. 4, 51â58 (2019)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00382-1#ref-CR21" id="ref-link-section-d50938e3541">21</a></sup>, <i>R. multiflora</i> (<i>Rosa multiflora</i>)<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 22" title="Hibrand, S. L. et al. A high-quality genome sequence of Rosa chinensis to elucidate ornamental traits. Nat. Plants 4, 36â43 (2018)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00382-1#ref-CR22" id="ref-link-section-d50938e3552">22</a></sup>, and <i>R. occidentalis</i> (<i>Rubus occidentalis</i>)<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 18" title="Vanburen, R. et al. The genome of black raspberry (Rubus occidentalis). Plant J. 87, 535â547 (2016)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00382-1#ref-CR18" id="ref-link-section-d50938e3562">18</a></sup>, were compared with each other using BLASTP, with a maximal E-value of 10<sup>â05</sup>. Markov chain clustering was performed by all-to-all analysis. The proteins predicted from all species with sequence lengths &gt;100 amino acids were queried against the Pfam database using Pfam scan<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 77" title="El, G. S. et al. The Pfam protein families database in 2019. Nucleic Acids Res. 47, 427â432 (2019)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00382-1#ref-CR77" id="ref-link-section-d50938e3569">77</a></sup>. The profiles of gene family expansion, contraction, and rapid evolution were analyzed by comparing the differences between the ancestor and each species using CAFE v4.0<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 81" title="De, B. T. et al. CAFE: a computational tool for the study of gene family evolution. Bioinformatics 22, 1269â1271 (2006)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00382-1#ref-CR81" id="ref-link-section-d50938e3573">81</a></sup>. Each gene module was extracted, and its contents were subjected to GO and KEGG functional enrichment analyses. There are usually multiple transcripts present for one gene, and only the longest transcript of each gene obtained from all of the species was considered a single-copy ortholog. The orthologous and paralogous genes of the protein datasets were condensed by removing redundancy via OrthoMCL v2.0.9<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 82" title="Li, L., Stoeckert, C. J. &amp; Roos, D. S. OrthoMCL: identification of ortholog groups for eukaryotic genomes. Genome Res. 13, 2178â2189 (2003)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00382-1#ref-CR82" id="ref-link-section-d50938e3577">82</a></sup>.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading c-article__sub-heading--divider" id="Sec21">Phylogenetic analysis</h3><p>Protein alignments with gaps removed for each single-copy gene family were acquired using the programs MAFFT<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 83" title="Katoh, K. &amp; Standley, D. M. MAFFT multiple sequence alignment software version 7: improvements in performance and usability. Mol. Biol. Evol. 30, 772â780 (2013)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00382-1#ref-CR83" id="ref-link-section-d50938e3589">83</a></sup> and trimAL<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 84" title="Capella, G. S., Silla, M. &amp; GabaldÃ³n, T. trimAl: a tool for automated alignment trimming in large-scale phylogenetic analyses. Bioinformatics 25, 1972â1973 (2009)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00382-1#ref-CR84" id="ref-link-section-d50938e3593">84</a></sup>. The best substitution model for the alignment was estimated using ModelFinder<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 85" title="Kalyaanamoorthy, S., Minh, B. Q., Wong, T. K., Von, H. A. &amp; Jermiin, L. S. ModelFinder: fast model selection for accurate phylogenetic estimates. Nat. Methods 14, 587â592 (2017)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00382-1#ref-CR85" id="ref-link-section-d50938e3597">85</a></sup>, with the default settings. The single-copy orthologous genes generated were aligned to a superalignment matrix with the guidance of protein alignment using MUSCLE 3.8.31<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 86" title="Edgar, R. C. MUSCLE: multiple sequence alignment with high accuracy and high throughput. Nucleic Acids Res. 32, 1792â1797 (2004)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00382-1#ref-CR86" id="ref-link-section-d50938e3601">86</a></sup>. A phylogenetic tree comprising <i>C. serrulata</i> and eight related species, <i>C. avium</i><sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 12" title="Shirasawa, K. et al. The genome sequence of sweet cherry (Prunus avium) for use in genomics-assisted breeding. DNA Research. 24, 499â508 (2017)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00382-1#ref-CR12" id="ref-link-section-d50938e3611">12</a></sup>, <i>P. persica</i><sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 13" title="Verde, I. et al. The high-quality draft genome of peach (Prunus persica) identifies unique patterns of genetic diversity, domestication and genome evolution. Nat. Genet. 45, 487â494 (2013)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00382-1#ref-CR13" id="ref-link-section-d50938e3617">13</a></sup>, <i>P. dulcis</i><sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 15" title="Velasco, D. et al. Evolutionary genomics of peach and almond domestication. G3 32, 116â121 (2016)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00382-1#ref-CR15" id="ref-link-section-d50938e3623">15</a></sup>, <i>P. mume</i><sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 20" title="Zhang, Q. et al. The genome of Prunus mume. Nat. Commun. 3, 1318â1325 (2012)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00382-1#ref-CR20" id="ref-link-section-d50938e3629">20</a></sup>, <i>P. yedoensis</i><sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 19" title="Seunghoon, B. et al. Draft genome sequence of wild Prunus yedoensis reveals massive inter-specific hybridization between sympatric flowering cherries. Genome Biol. 19, 45â51 (2018)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00382-1#ref-CR19" id="ref-link-section-d50938e3636">19</a></sup>, <i>R. chinensis</i><sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 21" title="Lin, W. et al. Characterization of the complete chloroplast genome of Chinese rose, Rosa chinensis (Rosaceae: Rosa). Mitochondrial DNA B. 4, 51â58 (2019)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00382-1#ref-CR21" id="ref-link-section-d50938e3642">21</a></sup>, <i>R. multiflora</i><sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 22" title="Hibrand, S. L. et al. A high-quality genome sequence of Rosa chinensis to elucidate ornamental traits. Nat. Plants 4, 36â43 (2018)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00382-1#ref-CR22" id="ref-link-section-d50938e3648">22</a></sup>, and <i>R. occidentalis</i><sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 18" title="Vanburen, R. et al. The genome of black raspberry (Rubus occidentalis). Plant J. 87, 535â547 (2016)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00382-1#ref-CR18" id="ref-link-section-d50938e3654">18</a></sup>, was constructed using PhyML v3.0<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 87" title="Guindon, S. et al. New algorithms and methods to estimate maximum-likelihood phylogenies: assessing the performance of PhyML 3.0. Syst. Biol. 59, 307â321 (2010)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00382-1#ref-CR87" id="ref-link-section-d50938e3659">87</a></sup> with the default parameters and <i>A. thaliana</i><sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 61" title="Meyerowitz, E. M. Arabidopsis thaliana. Ann. Rev. Genet. 21, 93â111 (2003)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00382-1#ref-CR61" id="ref-link-section-d50938e3665">61</a></sup> as an outgroup. The recommended divergence time from a fossil was obtained from the TimeTree database, and a molecular clock was employed to date the divergence event using PAML v4.8<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 88" title="Yang, Z. H. PAML 4: phylogenetic analysis by maximum likelihood. Mol. Biol. Evol. 24, 1586â1591 (2007)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00382-1#ref-CR88" id="ref-link-section-d50938e3669">88</a></sup> with the approximate likelihood calculation method.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading c-article__sub-heading--divider" id="Sec22">Whole-genome duplication (WGD) analysis</h3><p>In general, the ratio of the nonsynonymous substitution rate (<i>K</i>a) and the synonymous substitution rate (<i>K</i>s) was used to assess gene selection. Protein sequences of homologous genes from <i>C. serrulata</i> vs. those of representative species were aligned using MUSCLE<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 86" title="Edgar, R. C. MUSCLE: multiple sequence alignment with high accuracy and high throughput. Nucleic Acids Res. 32, 1792â1797 (2004)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00382-1#ref-CR86" id="ref-link-section-d50938e3691">86</a></sup>. As input files, the sequences of the homologous genes were imported into the KaKs Calculator to calculate the gene pair values. Positively selected genes in which <i>K</i>a/<i>K</i>sâ&gt;â1 were subsequently selected. In addition, CDS alignments obtained from previous protein sequence alignments were used to detect WGD based on the 4DTv values using the HKY model.</p></div></div></section>
